ROUGOL Meeting on Monday 19th Jan 2026

(date: 2026-01-14)

SUBJECT: Multi headed systems

This month Chris Hall will be Zooming in to show off his multiple heads. He has been experimenting with an R-Comp Hydra system, with two heads running RISC OS and a third with Linux.

He will be describing how well the new Hydra works, why he wanted multiple heads, how each head is configured, and how the system as a whole performs in use. He will expand on his article in the latest Archive, with a digression about RDP versus VNC for connecting between heads.

There should be time to look at some of his software ‚Äì such as RingBind, Cat, DrawDis and Locking, all of which make use of MakeDraw. He will demonstrate how to make subtle changes to Draw files that aren‚Äôt possible in Draw, by disassembling them using MultiTask and recreating them using MakeDraw after some subtle edits.

@Bryan your email at helpful demon co uk is not responding. Is Thur evening OK for a practice run please.

Updating Submenu Dialogue Boxes

(date: 2026-01-13)

I have a feeling that I might be missing something obvious here‚Ä¶

I have a dialogue box as a submenu (a program information window), which has a toggle size icon so that the user can expand it to read additional details about the application. This works fine.

However, it would be nice if it could always open in the small state, to be a little bit tidier. With a normal window, this would just be a case of fiddling with the visible extent before calling Wimp_OpenWindow, but as a submenu, I can‚Äôt see how to do it.

I can set the submenu warning flag and catch Message_SubmenuWarning, but as far as I know that gives me the window handle and not the Open Window block. Similarly, Wimp_CreateSubmenu doesn‚Äôt take anything but the handle, so I can‚Äôt mess with the visible area before creating the dialogue on screen.

Sitting on Open Window events for the dialogue suggests that the application doesn‚Äôt receive one until the window is moved, not when it initially opens ‚Äì so that doesn‚Äôt appear to help either.

Is there any way to achieve what I‚Äôm trying to do? Or is it a case of ‚ÄúI wouldn‚Äôt start from here‚Äù, and I need another approach to displaying the additional info (or just live with the toggled state persisting between visits)?

rustc, ELF, ld...

(date: 2026-01-12)

Found it!

rustc main.rs --target=armv7a-none-eabi -Clink-arg=--entry=_start -Clink-arg=-Tbaremetal.script

arm-none-eabi-objcopy  -R .ignoring -O binary main main,ff8 && od -t x4 -A x main,ff8

baremetal.script as above.

main.rs:

#![no_std]
#![no_main]

use core::arch::asm;
use core::arch::naked_asm;
use core::panic::PanicInfo;

// pub extern "C" to allow the naked asm to call main (with a stack).
#[no_mangle]
pub extern "C" fn main() {
  writec( b'H' );
  writec( b'e' );
  writec( b'l' );
  writec( b'l' );
  writec( b'o' );
  writec( b' ' );
  writec( b'w' );
  writec( b'o' );
  writec( b'r' );
  writec( b'l' );
  writec( b'd' );
  writec( 10 );
}

#[panic_handler]
fn panic_handler(_p: &PanicInfo) -> ! {
  loop {};
}

fn writec( c: u8 ) {
  unsafe {
    asm! ( "mov r0, {0}\n svc 0", in(reg) c );
  }
}

#[unsafe(link_section = ".init")]
#[no_mangle]
#[unsafe(naked)]
pub extern "C" fn _start() {
  naked_asm! (
         "mov r0, #0",
      "\n mov r1, #0",
      "\n mov r2, #0",
      "\n mov r3, #0",
      "\n svc 0x40",
      "\n mov sp, r1",
      "\n bl main",
      "\n svc 0x11"
      );
}

It‚Äôs untested, but the object code appears correct:

000000 e3a00000 e3a01000 e3a02000 e3a03000    Set r0-r3 to 0
000010 ef000040 e1a0d001 eb000003 ef000011    OS_ChangeEnvironment, set SP, call main, OS_Exit on return
000020 e1a00000 ef000000 e12fff1e e92d4800    writec r0 = c, OS_WriteC, return; main: push {fp, lr}
000030 e24dd008 e3a00048 ebfffff8 e3a00065    sub sp, sp, #8 (for no apparent reason), writec( 'H' 0x48 )
000040 ebfffff6 e3a0006c e58d0004 ebfffff3    writec( 'e' 0x65 ); writec( 'l' 0x6c ); ...
000050 e59d0004 ebfffff1 e3a0006f e58d0000
000060 ebffffee e3a00020 ebffffec e3a00077
000070 ebffffea e59d0000 ebffffe8 e3a00072
000080 ebffffe6 e59d0004 ebffffe4 e3a00064
000090 ebffffe2 e3a0000a ebffffe0 e28dd008    ... add sp, sp, #8
0000a0 e8bd8800 7fffff5c 00000001 7ffffff8    pop {fp, pc} (return); then 4 words .ARM.exidx
0000b0 00000001                                                      (whatever that is)

I wonder if the language requires 16-byte stack alignment (it would explain the sp +/- 8).

It doesn‚Äôt run on a RiscPC, uses bx lr 0xe12fff1e.

'Mailbox is full' phishing puzzle

(date: 2026-01-12)

I received an email yesterday saying:

==>

This message was created automatically by mail delivery software.

A message that you sent could not be delivered to one or more of its

recipients. This is a permanent error. The following address(es) failed:

info@theworkshopseries.co.uk LMTP error after RCPT TO:< info@theworkshopseries.co.uk >: 552 5.2.2 < info@theworkshopseries.co.uk > Mailbox is full / Blocks limit exceeded / Inode limit exceeded

Reporting-MTA: dns; s3161.fra1.stableserver.net

Action: failed

Final-Recipient: rfc822; info@theworkshopseries.co.uk

Status: 5.0.0

‚Ä¶.

<==

It is lying, because my message did get through to the intended recipient, who said that his mailbox

was certainly not full. Now I have heard of these ‚ÄòMailbox full‚Äô phishing scams. But the links in this

message appear to be harmless. I presume that the scam‚Äôs method relies on inserting malware into a

computer to take note of the sender-addresses of emails arriving in the inbox. I had used Plusnet‚Äôs

webmail to send my original email, using the Chrome browser, so I do not think there is any malware

inserted at my end. So no harm done. But is my diagnosis correct? Should I be warning

info@theworkshopseries.co.uk that his computer may have been compromised?

NAS problem

(date: 2026-01-10)

It shows ‚Äúsystem started to shut down due to auto poweroff time up‚Äù

Just putting that phrase into google comes up with this as the second link.

2019 thread https://community.synology.com/enu/forum/1/post/126798

‚ÄúI had the same issue and I just found what was the root cause in my case.

In ‚ÄúHardware and Power‚Äù ‚Äî> ‚ÄúHDD Hibernation‚Äù I had options ‚ÄúEnable advance HDD Hibernation‚Äù and ‚ÄúDS will enter standby via WOL after the HDD has hibernated‚Äù both checked.

This caused the NAS to power off, or maybe just to enter standby, but it did not wake up by itself, simply accessing the storage of through the web interface. I removed the ‚Äúenter standby‚Äù flag and everything works fine for me now."

Sponsorship for 64-bit work

(date: 2026-01-09)

Hiya,

There‚Äôs been a little bit of discussion about how people who are not technical can contribute towards work. One of the ways that has been suggested has been to provide donations towards people or that work. To try to provide a mechanism for this, I‚Äôve decided to use the GitHub Sponsorship button.

On many of my GitHub projects, including the general `riscos64-status` project ( https://github.com/gerph/riscos64-status), there is a Sponsor button. This will take you to https://github.com/sponsors/gerph/ where you can provide a sponsorship.

Providing sponsorship will encourage more development and tools for this project.

If you feel that the things that I‚Äôm doing and the work towards RISC OS 64 is valuable, please feel free to sponsor me!

Weird issue setting up printers

(date: 2026-01-08)

In case it matters, StrongED on the working machine is 4.68f12, while on the newer one it is 4.70a15, Has printing changed there?

Firstly, do you mean 4.68f2 (last version of 4.68) or 4.69f12?

I‚Äôve compared the printing code in 4.69f14 vs 4.70a20 and there aren‚Äôt that many differences. There‚Äôs some changes to how headers and footers are handled, and changes to make the print dbox override of the mode font height/width work.

If you‚Äôre using headers/footers then try turning them off and see if that helps.

ISTR an earlier report of PS3 issues but I can‚Äôt find that right now. Anyway, try printing with the PS2 driver, if possible. That will show if there is an issue with PS3 or if it‚Äôs a more generic problem.

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/11/topics/20207

Iyonix and the rest of my Risc OS collection

(date: 2026-01-08)

Firstly, don‚Äôt tick ‚Äúact as IP router‚Äù. If you fill in anything in the Routing window, only put the address of your router ‚Äì leave everything else blank. If using DHCP, leave everything blank/unticked.

For IP address, either use DHCP (no options) or static (fixed) IP address within same range as router (eg. 192.168.8.100). Netmask of 255.255.255.0 Note that not many routers use 192.168.8.x so you might want to confirm that. 192.168.1.x or 192.168.0.x are more common.

For Host names, put hostname (eg. iyonix) in first box.

If using DHCP leave rest unticked/blank.

If not using DHCP, put something in domain (must have a dot in it) such as .nom or .home or a full domain if you have one (eg. riscos.com). For primary DNS, put address of router. For secondary address put 1.1.1.1 (Cloudflare) or 8.8.8.8 (Google).

Set/Save etc. Don‚Äôt forget to reboot.

If this doesn‚Äôt work, be aware that one of the first signs of a failing Iyonix PSU is the network port failing. USB ethernet is possible on RISC OS ‚Äì stick to USB 2 adapters though, ideally with ASIX AX88772 chipset. Not every ROM has EtherUSB in ROM though.

RISC OS cannot use USB soundcards at all without a custom ROM. Even then, it can‚Äôt use it system-wide, only via specific software.

Finally, be aware that Iyonixes are amongst the more troublesome machines to keep going (see Martin Eastwood‚Äôs problems). You may be better off with a cheap Raspberry Pi to play around with ‚Äì it will likely give you better compatibility with old games etc via !ADFFS and the AnyMode module.

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/11/topics/20206

Developers‚Äô fireside chat ‚Äì 10th January

(date: 2026-01-07)

The opportunity has once again come around for people involved or interested in software development on, for, or even of RISC OS to gather together and discuss matters relevant to the topic. The next friendly fireside chat is scheduled to take place on Saturday, 10th January. The meetings ‚Äì which are held online, using the Zoom video conferencing system ‚Äì don‚Äôt follow a set agenda. Instead, the discussion topics are down to those people present, and what they wish to bring up or ask about. For example, at the last‚Ä¶

https://www.riscository.com/2026/developers-fireside-chat-10th-january/

Coding on RISC OS fireside chat, Saturday 10th Jan.

(date: 2026-01-07)

App locations inside !Boot

(date: 2026-01-06)

I‚Äôm beginning to delve into the murky innards of !Boot, with a view to extending the Clarity theme to the various default apps within it, including Configure. Presently, the sprites in the Clarity theme are installed with a simple Boot merge, with the new files all added into !Boot.Resources.!ThemeDefs.Themes.Clarity. This ensures that the sprites used by the Wimp, plus the icons used for the ROM Apps, are replaced.

If I also want to replace the icons used for the various !Boot apps (!Scrap, !System, etc), then I‚Äôm assuming that I can use the same Boot merge to add the required sprites into their various application directories (ie, !Boot.Resources.!System.Themes.Clarity, etc). This does assume that those application directories never move around ‚Äì is that something I can rely on?

Similarly, the icons for the Configure app aren‚Äôt all in the same place. On RO5.31, most are in !Boot.RO500Hook.Res.Configure, but the Internet configuration seems to live in !Boot.Resources.Configure. Again, can I rely on these locations staying consistent, and use a Boot merge to add new sprites into their respective app directories?

I‚Äôm aware that there are theme manager applications in development, such as ExtTheme, that will probably be able to handle all this with a bit more aplomb, but I‚Äôm hoping to keep the basic distribution of Clarity as simple as possible ‚Äì just an iconset that can be copied over !Boot with the various components dropped into the right places.

Celebrate ten years of the Titanium with WROCC ‚Äì 7th January

(date: 2026-01-04)

Back in October 2015, there was a surprise announcement something visitors to that year‚Äôs London Show could expect to see ‚Äì a new motherboard, designed by Rob Sprowson, with RISC OS in mind; the Titanium. The board itself became available through Rob‚Äôs company Elesar Ltd in December of that year, allowing people to build DIY machines around it, and it wasn‚Äôt long before there were complete Titanium-based computer systems available from both R-Comp and CJE Micro‚Äôs. That was a touch over a decade ago, and Rob Sprowson will be taking‚Ä¶

Live Coding with Gerph, Sunday 4th January at 1pm UK time.

(date: 2026-01-04)

A bit of a scattered day today. I had fixed PicoC so that it could handle the _IN() and _OUT() macros, but somehow broke _OUTR() so the testing got a little distracted. However, the SWIs all seem to work on RISC OS 64, and so I moved on to replacing the data blob for the CPU registers descriptions with one that can be generated. We now have some Python code that builds the data that these tables use, which will make it a lot easier when we need to replace them with a different platform (or update them!).

Hopefully that was interesting to people. I also showed off the hotkey lookup in the editor as well ‚Äì pressing shift-ctrl-h opens a Chrome Window with the relevant RISC OS documentation in. Pretty simple to do with all the other work that‚Äôs gone before, but I finally got around to doing it.

With that, I think I‚Äôm done on what I want to do on the Kernel Introspection for now ‚Äì it‚Äôs stubbed well enough. I think next week, I think I‚Äôm going to have a look at FSCommands, unless anyone wants to jump in and ask for one of the other components‚Ä¶

Most of Phase 1 is complete ( https://github.com/gerph/riscos64-status/wiki/Phase-1) but Phase 2 has lots of things in it ( https://github.com/gerph/riscos64-status/wiki/Phase-2).

(date: 2026-01-03)

Hiya,

Just a little note to say that the PicoC tool that I‚Äôve been using for some of the verification of 32-bit and 64-bit components has been released. PicoC is an interpreted C, which you can use at the command line or with files. It‚Äôs handy for writing small things in which just exercise a few SWI calls.

It is even passing its almost all the original tests that were supplied with it (those not run are largely for time).

New DME ExtTheme and Launchpad available for download and testing

(date: 2026-01-02)

Thanks Chris, hope you‚Äôll like your old protocol still living, breathing and growing, now The Little Yellow Moon original protocol also works for themes from boot :)

Meanwhile:

Big thanks to Martin for testing new themes creation and also running this on his own systems.

I have pushed a new build that implements it‚Äôs own file copying in C, because calling RISC OS `*Copy` via OS_CLI in a Task Window from an Application doesn‚Äôt seems to be very reliable on RO 5.31 if themes are a bit big (on the multiple megabytes size). Anyway the new in-app copy implementation is a lot more reliable, hence installing zipped themes from a TaskWindow should be fine now.

Also, I pushed a new build of the dark theme, because the previous one was missing the font. (Yes ExtTheme can install Theme‚Äôs fonts too).

Note: !PackMan replace the app when updating, so, my DME will create a backup copy of your old one in `Boot:Resources.DME_Backups`, so if you feel like your installed themes have disapeared after an update you can find them in the safety backup and/or you can simply install them again via `*theme install ‚Ä¶`.

A note for Andrew/ROD, it seems that Iris had some issues downloading zip files (the themes), the same zips download fine with NetSurf. I am still figuring what‚Äôs going on with Iris, so consider this an heads up only for now (and if you are around and reading this).

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/1/topics/20199

Using EX0 and EY0 for higher definition

(date: 2026-01-02)

There are a quite a few things that don‚Äôt take into account the screen scaling when using EX0 EY0. The mouse pointer is one of them.

The OS does scale the mouse pointer for the eigen factors, witness changing to a EX1 EY2 mode. The issue is that a number of APIs assume no more than 32√ó32 hardware cursor (probably arising from VIDC, but I think some other graphics controllers have that limit too) so for example when you try to scale ptr_default which is 22 pixels high at EX1 EY1 you‚Äôd get 44 pixels at EX0 EY0 and the bottom 12 pixels are cropped off. The hourglass with percentage is taller still.

So your options are:

  • Live with the cropped pointer. Result: at least it‚Äôs proportionally the right size compared with everything else
  • Fudge it by using the 12√ó22 pixel pointer sprite in the Wimp‚Äôs Sprites11 file, this is what Castle opted to do with the Iyonix and that‚Äôs spread to some of the other themes. Result: at least it‚Äôs not cropped, just a bit teeny tiny
  • Roll up your sleeves and ripple the planned API changes through all the bits of low level graphics drivers which assume 32√ó32. Result: not cropped and correctly scaled on hardware that can do bigger overlays
https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/11/topics/20200

List of modules in C

(date: 2026-01-01)

It relies on parts of the C library, which makes it problematic. StubsG is available as a binary and works ‚Äì it should be usable as-is. Is there a particular issue you have found with the library?

The C library‚Äôs Apache licensed, so as long as you‚Äôre willing to make your code have a compatible licence it should be fine.

If it‚Äôs of interest, I have a (macOS/Linux) Makefile that fetches the source for stubs and builds three variants ‚Äì 26bit, 32bit and vfp. The latter is a 32-bit stubs, patched automatically. It uses a python (extended) implementation of decaof to rename certain symbols in the symbol table in the .o files, and includes in the library veneers. These veneers export the original function name, and call the renamed functions. And they‚Äôre all made into a library with a python reimplementation of libfile. It sounds like it works very similarly to StubsG?

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/13/topics/20164

USBDriver vulnerability

(date: 2026-01-01)

Hi Matthew, happy new year!

That sounds annoying. Please do

*Set Debugger$AnnotatedFile $.excdump
*Set Debugger$DumpOptions -file annotated

and then after the crash you should find an excdump file which tells you which function 5b18 actually is in your USBDriver plus a backtrace. You could either post it here or attach it to a bug report in the bugs section of this website.

RISC OS today and tomorrow: understanding behaviour and trade-offs

(date: 2025-12-30)

I modified QEMU to load the ‚Äúbios‚Äù (RISC OS ROM image) at 0 instead of 0√ó8000/0√ó80000. So it behaves like kernel_old=1 in config.txt (iirc).

#define FIRMWARE_ADDR_2 0 // 0x8000 /* Pi 2 loads kernel.img here by default */
#define FIRMWARE_ADDR_3 0 // 0x80000 /* Pi 3 loads kernel.img here by default */

Plus a bunch of excessive logging, but that‚Äôs another matter.

If I were them, I‚Äôd have gone for a -preload file,address option, myself, to cover all eventualities like bios, kernel, inird, etc..

Just out of interest, do you do anything with ATAGs? I leave a gap, they‚Äôll be readable, but I don‚Äôt scan them yet.

Is the system heap meant to be writable from BASIC?

(date: 2025-12-27)

I was just thinking about somewhere safe for privileged code to write to for user mode code to read from and thought perhaps the system heap, since that‚Äôs where I thought the system variables are stored (and R3 returned from OS_ReadVarVal points to).

So I tried:

SYS"XOS_ReadVarVal", "*", 0, -1, 0, 0 TO ,,,V%

V% is set to &303FF7CC, in the system heap, not RMA (&20000000) and printing the string there shows ‚Äú7backup\(Dir‚Äù, as expected. What I wasn‚Äôt expecting was `V%?5=42` to work, let alone change the name of the variable to ‚Äú7back\*p\)Dir‚Äù!

Is this a limitation of recent MMUs?

Firstly, I‚Äôd like to wish everyone a Happy Christmas and a super, RISC OS-filled 2026. Thankyou to eveyone for being part of the community this year, and for all your RISC OS related activity, support, developments, purchases and forum posts etc.

I‚Äôm now finishing for Christmas (well, it is nearly 4pm on Christmas Eve). The intention is to take a bit of a longer Christmas break as I‚Äôm absolutely exhausted from a non-stop year. I‚Äôve been working weekends since the summer, and still not found time to celebrate my birthday from back in October! We‚Äôve more-or-less cleared the decks in time for Christmas, so the plan is to take a rest until early Jan.

BASIC and LOCAL DATA

(date: 2025-12-24)

In PDP11 BASIC it took just one extra instruction to fix LOCALDATA:continue tokenising:

jsr  pc,TokenSearch	; Search token table
;...
bit  #2,r2		; Are we at the start of statement?
bne  TokenWord1		; No, enter token/char
bit  #16,r1		; Is this a pseudo-variable?
beq  TokenWord2		; No, enter unchanged
add  #&40,r0		; Convert token to command token
.TokenWord1
bic  #&40,r2		; *EXTRA* Middle of statement, don't turn tokeniser off
.TokenWord2
mov  r1,r2		; Copy new flags to current flags
;...

It looks to me that the ARM code would be similarly simple to update. I‚Äôll have a look at it over Christmas.

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/4/topics/19900

GCCSDK Built with Nix!

(date: 2025-12-23)

I‚Äôm pretty sure that I am the only person using GCCSDK via nix, but I‚Äôve got some updates!

Firstly, I‚Äôm using it to compile for RiscOS from an Apple Silicon Mac! It will also definitely work on windows using WSL! So if you are using any of those platforms, great news! This will work a charm!

Next, I‚Äôve managed to create an initial cross stdenv which means that it is much easier to use nix as the build system. The example flake is here:

https://github.com/yobson/riscos-nix/tree/main/example

Next steps will be building OSLib and others this way and move some things over from the auto builder. I also spotted the nordsoft compiler on GitHub (I don‚Äôt think it‚Äôs the one ROOL uses but will work for risc os), so I may give that the same treatment.

Either way, this is turning out to be a very nice way to bring building for risc os to 2025.

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/1/topics/19890

CRamFS

(date: 2025-12-19)

I finally got around to trying this out on the RiscPC (using a StrongARM and RISC OS 5.30), and have got some initial numbers from m1time:

RamFS 2.33 (23 Nov 2020):

Save 1M * 1000: 8539 csec

Load 1M * 1000: 6131 csec

CRamFS + memmove:

Save 1M * 1000: 9370 csec

Load 1M * 1000: 7028 csec

CRamFS + BlockMove:

Save 1M * 1000: 9517 csec

Load 1M * 1000: 6346 csec

I‚Äôve added a bunch of comments on the merge request of things that might help, but I currently don‚Äôt have any tools for getting more detailed benchmarks on the RiscPC. That said, it should be possible to get the performance roughly equivalent in C ‚Äì the BlockMove function seems to be the only part that‚Äôs doing something complicated that would require assembly code for performance.

Obscure wimp sprites

(date: 2025-12-16)

Some more thoughts on Paint, having been using it very heavily over the past few weeks:

  • The various bugs that used to affect various tools in the Sprite window seem to have been very effectively squashed. I don‚Äôt think I‚Äôve had a single crash from that source over many hours of use.
  • The new outline font tool is great, as is the much better Paintbrush interface. Very nice work.
  • There‚Äôs a bug report (ticket 520) open on the file dragging/selection in the Spritefile window. This issue would be great to look at ‚Äì it‚Äôs pretty annoying to drag a sprite into a file window and have it replace whatever is currently selected, even if the sprites have different names. When dragging dozens of files around, it‚Äôs very easy to overwrite stuff by mistake this way.
  • Relatedly, if you try to rename a sprite in a Spritefile window to one that already exists, Paint silently fails to rename it, rather than telling you why.
  • The only crashes I‚Äôve had came when deleting a sprite from a Spritefile window. Annoyingly, I can‚Äôt reproduce this reliably. If I can find some way to reproduce this, I‚Äôll file a ticket.

I‚Äôm not sure if the Bounty work is still current. If it is, then taking a look at some of these issues in the Spritefile window would be really useful. I think possible fixes here would be to:

  • Mimic the Filer‚Äôs selection behaviour, so that selecting sprites in one Spritefile window clears the previous selection in another window
  • Alternatively (or in addition), don‚Äôt overwrite selected sprites with different names when dragging sprite(s) into a Spritefile window, but just add the new sprites to the Spritefile
  • When a sprite or selection of sprites is dragged to a Spritefile window containing a sprite(s) with the same name, or the user tries to rename a sprite with a name already existing in the file, query the decision. Either halt it, or offer to skip/abort/overwrite.

In any case, congrats to Andy for all his hard work ‚Äì the app has been really transformed.

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/5/topics/20161

RPCEmu NAT fail.

(date: 2025-12-16)

Following the recent DDE update to DDE32b this issue is fixed in the IOMDROM of 14-Dec-25.

From the changelogs :-

Fix for loads of halfword values not making use of unaligned LDR instructions when they are permitted by -memaccess +L41. This resulted in the halfword being formulated from two LDRB instructions which the register allocator did not expect, and R12 being wrongly reused in some small leaf functions.

Accessing ROOL Via Three Broadband

(date: 2025-12-15)

You‚Äôre most likely on IPv4?

Very definitely on both IPv6 and IPv4. I was surprised when I tried a Three SIM and found it gave me an IPv6 address (not to be confused with what WiFi gives me!). The IPv6 support is the primary reason I moved (just a few days ago) from O2 to Three.

The killer test, which I‚Äôve just repeated, is to access one of my IPv6-only sites from my phone after turning WiFi off. The web page and the site‚Äôs log both show the Three IPv6 address of my phone, which has a very different prefix from that given to me by WiFi.

Live Coding with Gerph, Sunday 14th December at 1pm.

(date: 2025-12-15)

Yes, times posted on this site are invariably using UK local time. I‚Äôll include that note in the future, but you can always find out the timezone relative time by going to the YouTube link which should be accurate (unless I schedule stupidly). All my sessions have always been at 1pm UK time.

The session yesterday went quite well, despite feeling a little unwell through it. Implementation of the stubbed functions is progressing well. OS_Byte calls are stubbed, although I went back and forth on their naming, as they seem to be given different names in different places. OS_ReadSysInfo has about a third of the calls stubbed as well. We‚Äôre only getting a skeleton right now, so it‚Äôs not especially complicated.

Tests have been ported from RISC OS Pyromaniac and look ok ‚Äì they will need to change as we update the implementation.

Next week I‚Äôll look at the OS_Platform calls and probably the memory calls as well.

RDPclient with Windows 10

(date: 2025-12-13)

I‚Äôve just had the same issue with RDPClient connecting to a new install of Windows 11 Professional 25H2.

There were some additional settings that I needed to change to get RDPClient to connect. (I was seeing the same ‚Äúconnection reset by peer error‚Äù)

1. Open GPEDIT.MSC

2. Expand Computer Configuration > Administrative Templates > Windows Components > Remote Desktop Services > Remote Desktop Session Host > Security

3. Change ‚ÄúSet client connection encryption level‚Äù to ‚ÄúLOW‚Äù

4. Change "Require use of specific security layer for remote (RDP) connections to ‚ÄúRDP‚Äù

5. Change "Require user authentication for remote connections by using Network Level Authtication to ‚ÄúDISABLED‚Äù

6. Reboot the PC

Obviously lowering the security defaults for Remote Desktop is a bad idea security wise, so use at your own risk!

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/11/topics/20005

Status update for RISC OS 64-bit work

(date: 2025-12-12)

It‚Äôs been about 5 weeks since I did a status update on the 64-bit RISC OS work.

  • The Wimp Templates subcomponent was worked on as part of the Live Coding and is now complete ‚Äì See https://github.com/gerph/riscos-wimp-templates for the details.

  • The `riscos64-status` repository has been updated with a few things:

    • `PicoC` is noted as a ported language.
    • `Lua` is noted as a ported language.
    • `TCC` is noted as a ported implementation of a C compiler.
    • `GCC` was removed from the ported implementations (it‚Äôs not ported, but is usable to build for RISC OS 64, and had been misplaced).
    • `Pascal` is noted as a ported language (using the P2C tool).
    • `Rust` is noted as having been prototyped for use with RISC OS 64.
    • All the feature documents for component now include completion percentages on their pages.

  • The `Kernel: Modules` subcomponent had been started.

  • The `EvaluateExpression` module has been stubbed.

  • The `IIC` module has been stubbed.

  • The `OSSWIs` module has been stubbed.

  • The hourglass maker has been ported to RISC OS 64. See https://github.com/gerph/riscos-hourglass-maker for details.

    • The module can be found in the `riscos64-status` repository as with many others.

  • The Pascal-to-C implementation is being worked into the build environment.

  • I presented the general status of RISC OS 64 work to ROUGOL, and the presentation is available on YouTube and through my presentation site. See https://presentations.riscos.online/pyromaniac4/index.‚Ä¶ for video, slides and resource links.

  • RISC OS Pyromaniac screenshots and videos were updated with the details of the changes and work towards 64-bit. See https://pyromaniac.riscos.online/examples.html#talk2025 for images and videos.

  • The RISC OS 64-bit C library has been updated with better handling of linking hidden and internal symbols, and `fgetc` now works properly. See https://github.com/gerph/riscos64-clib for details.

  • `objasm2gas` tool has been updated to handle `:INDEX:` and `:BASE:` (as well as the `@` metavariable), and fix problems with field mappings using registers not being calculated as expressions.

  • The `Kernel: Introspection` component will be the next live coding project.

Anyhow, that‚Äôs where things are for me. You can always follow the repositories to see what‚Äôs being done.

As usual, if anyone wants to contribute to these, please speak up.

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/13/topics/20171

Setting up a new monitor

(date: 2025-12-10)

Proivde Simple 3D api to basic?

(date: 2025-12-09)

RISC OS already support OpenGL. This wish list item would be to provide a simple module translating GL or VUlkan(?) calls to an appropriate SWI. in BASIC you would then do SYS ‚ÄúGLFunc‚Äù,‚Äú@‚Äù, PTR param_block.

Where GLFunc gets 2 pointers, 1(string) to the name of OPenGL(ES) or Vulkan Function, and the second param being a sutiable width pointer to the parameter block.

Alternatively it would be nice to have some kind of native 3D api, that can be called directly from Basic.

A Puzzling Addition to the Platform

(date: 2025-12-08)

With uncharacteristic speed following the release of Puzzles 1.00 for RISC OS, version 1.01 is now available to download from https://www.stevefryatt.org.uk/risc-os/games ‚Äì copies can also be found on the PlingStore, and should appear in PackMan shortly.

The main changes from 1.00 are a few updates from the upstream ‚Äì the user-facing ones are to the Dominosa, Mines and Undead games.

The RISC OS front end now supports the text_fallback() function, which allows it to make the characters in the top half of the current RISC OS character set available to games if they wish to make use of them. This improves the text display in a couple of the puzzles. If you‚Äôre playing Puzzles on a platform that doesn‚Äôt support the UCS lookup tables, or are using an alphabet that doesn‚Äôt have the desired glyphs in it, then games will continue to use plain ASCII as before.

@AVB,

I wouldn‚Äôt bother. Pretty much every solution for running RISC OS applications supported sound. The ‚ÄòRISC OS On Linux‚Äô project, totally understandably, hasn‚Äôt got around to that yet. And if you are just using typical desktop apps, then it‚Äôs no big deal. We are talking about one implementation here, with what, a handful of users. I‚Äôd be stunned if it was worth the effort.

Also, I think for most games, the sound is key too.

If anyone wants to spend time on it, I‚Äôd suggest a module which accepts the relevant SWIs/vectors/whatever for the sound APIs, and just does nothing with them. That would allow audio apps/games to start. In the future, some enterprising soul can figure out how to glue the module into talking to the Linux audio API.

Frosted Icon Set for 2025

(date: 2025-11-26)

Ok guys,

let me disable the wobbly stuff (there are quite a few, because I started to reverse engineer WTB patch if anyone remebers it, to add it to my ExtTheme and allow even more customizability), I‚Äôll package it and give it to both of you for testing.

It should take me a few days max.

ExtTheme already has all your work Chris for your old Theme Manager, so you‚Äôll need to create a theme file with all the configuration options like you did in the past. The Theme file format is identical (I kept the same format for compatibility with the past Themes made for your TM). There are more options now, and it does work fine with coloring the windows border (well it can do even more than that, and add size to the border too, but that size is one of the wobbly functions).

It also already includes all the features of ThemeDef from ROOL, and everything is rewritten in C (‚Äôcause some folks complained that DME Launchpad was written in BBCBASIC‚Ä¶).

I‚Äôll need both your emails, please contact me at the link below, and as soon as I have disabled the things that makes RO unstable I‚Äôll send you a PackMan package that should install both the Configure UI and the Theme actuator.

Episode IV - A New Hope

(date: 2025-11-20)

Not only did 1977 see the release of space opera Star Wars ‚Äì A New Hope, but it was also a year famous for the release of Fortran 77, the follow up to Fortran IV and ‚Äô66.

Your compliance is imperative

Fortran is one of a family of imperative programming languages, and was originally short for For mula Tran slation. Finding applications in scientific fields such as modelling of weather systems, molecular structure, and of course calculating star ship propulsion vectors.

Image available as wallpaper from r33v01v3 via Steam

As described in our FAQ the imperative languages are in the class of languages that the Norcroft compiler supports, and we‚Äôve long known from odd scraps of evidence such as the RISC iX User Guide that there was a Fortran version at one time which went alongside the C language we‚Äôre so much more familiar with.

With help from Codemist a search of their archives managed to locate a partial copy last worked on in the 1990s on a backup tape stowed inside an old R2-unit.

Joining the Fortran front end ‚Äì the part of the compiler which deals with language specifics ‚Äì with the rest of the contemporary tools creates the f77 compiler. In addition, a brand new 200+ page manual describes its use in detail, along with ANSI runtime library.

https://www.riscosopen.org/news/articles/2025/11/20/episode-iv-a-new-hope

Time to Update !Killer :)

(date: 2025-11-18)

A few things in no particular order.

  1. There was a security permissions ‚Äúgotcha‚Äù that we‚Äôd not spotted that came in during a gitlab update a few months ago that was preventing the automatic git mirroring occurring for the TCP/IP 6 project. This has now been resolved, so the code should now auto-update between the internal project git and the ROD git. As a result, the missing 7.09 code is now present as expected.

  2. AFAIK that auto-mirroring only applies to that specific project, and happens more-or-less in realtime, so should always reflect latest code. Those wishing to contribute should contact us for further info. Other project repositories work as you would normally expect.

  3. Vprotect and Killer sources are now in the ROD git. However, they are not publicly visible due to concerns over security, and there not being enough remaining skilled coders to provide the necessary levels of peer review.

  4. My goal would be for public binary builds to appear ASAP

  5. Access to those git repositories is available on request, but it is likely we will vet applicants to at least some degree because of the sensitivity of the materials. We have already had one compelling offer to provide long term maintenance of this software, but I‚Äôm aware other work has been done and am keen to see all interested parties working together on this.

  6. The hint about the Explore link was in the ‚ÄúExplore the github‚Äù but you can do so directly via https://gitlab.riscosdev.com/explore

  7. Don‚Äôt expect to see the Vprotect/Killer projects in the public ‚Äúexplore‚Äù due to their sensitivity, until such time as releases are ready.

This is why KeyPress must be interpreted in the current Alphabet.

Why is ROOL doing this?

(date: 2025-11-15)

Ok, so maybe ‚Äòrandom‚Äô wasn‚Äôt strictly accurate, what I really do is use the same one swi allocation that was ever even approximately mine every time I write a module. From memory this includes the original use, a podule rom board to boot NFS, A broken driver for DE600 parallel Ethernet interface, a dot1Q vlan encapsulation layer (also broken) a driver for a bbc Winchester or Filestore drive on a Arc 1MHze bus podule, or more recently a DCI 4 implementation of the DCI2 ip over econet encapsulation, so I think I will get away with it for a while yet.

Clearly a web site you make an account on, confirm you email, upload the !Allocate file, which at least proves you are reasonably ligit, and emails you back and displays on the web page, would be very much better.

Toolbox File Format

(date: 2025-11-13)

Yes, though remember Gadget is a variable size depending on the gadget. The original Toolbox manual describes it the best as it highlights various pitfalls.

Set num_gadgets and they then go sequentially in the ‚Äòdata‚Äô field. Each gadget has a size, which is (usually) the offset to the next gadget.

http://www.riscos.com/support/developers/toolbox/windo‚Ä¶

http://www.riscos.com/support/developers/toolbox/windo‚Ä¶

The pitfalls are that you shouldn‚Äôt assume the size of each header (ie. Window template or Gadget template) and instead use the offsets ‚ÄúThe use of a body_offset field is to allow expansion in the header, without losing backwards compatibility.‚Äù Similarly ‚Äògadgets‚Äô is an offset, in the Window template, and ‚Äútype/size‚Äù has the gadget size in the gadget top two bytes (the second link above describes ‚Äútype/size‚Äù).

For reading a file, you should handle the offsets properly, but the reality is they are just memory dumps of the C structures that have never changed size.

Annoyingly, it says ‚ÄúNote that for the gadgets listed below, the size is ‚Äòbuilt in‚Äô to the Window module, and so the size can be set to zero‚Ä¶‚Äù which is ridiculous, so means you‚Äôll have to hard-code the sizes for the original gadget set. I think you should use the built-in size if the value in the file is zero, and the value in the file if it‚Äôs non-zero.

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/5/topics/20118

RPCEmu inside Docker, using VNC

(date: 2025-11-12)

The article today about using RPCEmu on macOS reminded me that I‚Äôve not mentioned the Docker images for RPCEmu that I created some time ago since they were updated. It also made me finally add the automatic resizing and push a multi-arch image (coo, I can now do both ARM and AMD in the same image!).

To use‚Ä¶

docker run -it --rm -p 5901:5901 -v $PWD:/riscos/Shared gerph/rpcemu-3.7

or

docker run -it --rm -p 5901:5901 -v $PWD:/riscos/Shared gerph/rpcemu-5

then connect to the VNC server (with Screen Sharing, or some other client) at localhost:5901 and use the password password.

The current working directory is shared into $.Shared.

As this is a separate configuration, a clean system, and has access to the filesystem it‚Äôs really trivial to customise, or just use for running those odd things that you need now and then. And you can be sure that you‚Äôve not broken the system as it‚Äôs exactly as distributed.

The disc image is as supplied by the easy start bundles, with tiny tweaks (removing the Acorn logo from the backdrop, changing the screen mode to be larger, and adding a module that resizes the X server on mode change). This also has the interesting side effect of making the system rather more useable when made full screen.

And of course, being docker, you can also run this on Linux and on Windows, and it‚Äôll be pretty much the same.

Sources, as usual, are on GitHub ‚Äì https://github.com/gerph/rpcemu-docker. You can see the startlingly dumb way that the screen resolution is communicated out of the emulator in the VNCResize module. It‚Äôs certainly enough to work on the simple mode changes.

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/1/topics/20115

Floating Point in C

(date: 2025-11-11)

I‚Äôve got the score up over 900k, and once over 1m, by giving it more registers ‚Äì I chose to set the baseline to allow the output to run on a PiZero which only has 8 D VFP registers. But 8 D registers means (under AAPCS) none are preserved over a function call. Giving it more would clearly be more efficient, but limits the h/w it can run on. I see apcs-softpcs (which I copied for VFP init) requests 16 D registers.

Curiously, 4 saved D FP registers outperforms 6 or 7 saved (ie. in addition to the 8 D arg registers) ‚Äì I‚Äôll investigate more as that shouldn‚Äôt really happen. ARM‚Äôs Norcroft currently has a limit of 31 registers (int + FP), due to its impressive use of signed maths throughout, so I can‚Äôt easily use 8 + 8.

After a little bit of fiddling around ‚Ä¶ it now runs.

That‚Äôs quite neat. Potentially could be useful, in fact, since my regression test harness (running on unix) can‚Äôt execute any code under RISC OS, only check the disassembled output. I was pondering ELF output for a Pi, but I‚Äôve done all the work on a Mac (hence RPCEmu, hence forgetting about unaligned memory).

Modern, mainstream browsers tend to block insecure links/content in secure pages.

Yay, fewer spamages. It‚Äôs literally a one-line python http.server running as a very restricted user as I couldn‚Äôt be bothered to setup up a web server, but probably should one day.

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/11/topics/19431

Keyboard layout and *configure country

(date: 2025-11-10)

Looking at the RISC OS source, on reset the keyboard type is set to UK in KeyPostInit in Kernel/s/PMF/key. I have modified RISCOS.IMG so that this routine sets the type to USA instead of UK (by directly changing byte 0√ó458d4 of the RPi Stable 5.30 ROM image to 0√ó30, from 0√ó01 ‚Äì there doesn‚Äôt seem to be any checksum on this binary image on the Pi).

As a workaround, this seems fine ‚Äì now I have a default USA keyboard when booting directly to supervisor/BASIC.

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/4/topics/20108

Translating BASIC to C

(date: 2025-11-10)

Long term readers of these fora may remember that I think Printer Manager is far too big to be extended to deal with IPP printers in its present BASIC form.

It occurred to me that it might be possible to translate it to C, in small increments, leaving it testable at all times, by translating bottom-up (i.e. replacing the lowest level functions and procedures first) and replacing them with calls to a module written in C. The module would only be needed until all the translation is done, by which time we‚Äôd have a complete translation into C that then would be converted from a module to an app.

Printer Manager is an enormous job to take on top-down, as nothing could be used until it‚Äôs all done. The way I‚Äôm suggesting would have something testable and usable (the ultimate test of testability!) at all stages.

Any thoughts?

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/3/topics/20112

Guide to Impression

(date: 2025-11-07)

The Guide to the Impression Suite now comes with a complete worked example of how to turn a document into a RindBind manual. It starts with an Impression Publisher document which is the original manual for Equasor, TableMate etc. that was originally created in Impression. The process to print that as a PDF, then to extract individual Draw files for each page from that PDF is described in detail with examples at each stage. Packaging this into a ‚ÄòRingBind‚Äô file is also described in detail with all the files created at each stage provided. As RingBind reserves space for the Draw file data for four pages, each the size of the largest individual Draw file for a page, it makes sense to reduce the few largest Draw files to a resolution appropriate to screen display rather than printing. The process to do this is also described. A copy of MakeDraw is required.

BBC BASIC - Simple OOP Extensions

(date: 2025-11-06)

I have always thought that BBCBASIC needed records.

RTR‚Äôs BASICs have Structures, but the syntax doesn‚Äôt really feel native to BBCBASIC.

I have been a fan of Wirth‚Äôs Oberon with type extension of records as it is a clean simple concept.

Most OO languages go off into the weeds with very complex and subtle features that are not really needed for 99% of programs.

I have outlined a possible syntax/semantics for a simplified OOP style record structure description below.

Let me know what you think.

OUTLINE OF CONCEPT:

Defininng a record type

No Args (fixed size)

DEF RECmyrec

A% // Integer field

B // Floating field

C$ // String field

D@ // Pointer field (any RECxxx) initial value NULL

DIM E% 1024 // Raw byte block field 1kB inline in record, use with indirection operators

DIM F%(9) // Array of 10 ints

DIM G(9) // Array of 10 floats

DIM H$(9) // Array of 10 strings

DIM I@(9) // Array of 10 pointer to record initial value NULL

ENDREC

With Args (variable size and initial values)

DEF RECmyvarrec(n$,m%,blocksize%)

name\( = n\) // Initialise value

DIM list$(m%) // n+1 strings ‚Äì record contains a pointer to the array

DIM block% blocksize%*2+38 // can do calculations; specifies number of bytes, numbered 0 to result-1

ENDREC

Global or Private

R@ = RECmyrec // Globals use the heap (I would prefer if the language had GLOBAL to specify global varsfor symmetry/clarity)

// this version of the creation syntax does not make it obvious that allocation is taking place here

GLOBAL R@ = RECmyrec // opt global designator

R@ = NEW RECobject // alternetive syntax choice for creating a new record, makes it explicit that record allocation is taking place.

PRIVATE T@ = NEW RECmyrec // PRIVATEs use the heap. Same as PRIVATE in RTRBBCBASIC

STATIC ‚Äî used for ‚Äúclass variables/methods‚Äù see below

I prefer the use of NEW rather than DIM because DIM is already used for Arrays and Structures

Stack (LOCAL vars)

LOCAL S@ = NEW RECmyvarrec(‚ÄúBob‚Äù,9,256) // Locals also use the heap because we will often export the reference from the scope expecting the record to persist.

When LOCAL pointer variable goes out of scope, the pointer on the stack is deleted, but the record (on heap) remains and may cause memory leaks,

CLEANUP should be used periodically.

If it is known that the record is no longer needed, it should be deleted before it goes out of scope.

The interpreter could detect escaping references and delete those that don‚Äôt, this can be complex with subtle errors, so manual or GC is easier.

Alternatively use Reference Counting (simpler, but risks memory leaks)

Delete Records and Release Heap Memory (manual GC)

DEL p@ ‚Äî frees the storage fields (strings, arrays, blocks) then frees the record, does NOT follow pointer fields.

CLEANUP ‚Äî executed outside any PROC or FN, marks all records reachable via global and private pointer variables then sweeps unmarked heap, does NOT follow pointers stored in Raw byte data blocks.

Method:

Add all global & static pointers to the keep queue

While keep queue not empty

‚Ä¶.Pull the next pointer from the keep queue as current record

‚Ä¶.If current record not marked

‚Ä¶‚Ä¶..Add all pointers to records to the keep queue

‚Ä¶‚Ä¶..Mark current record for retention

Sweep the record heap freeing all unmarked records using the DEL operation above.

DELREC q@ ‚Äî as DEL above, BUT it also follows pointer chains deleting all linked records, does NOT follow pointers stored in Raw byte data blocks.

Method:

Add q@ to the delete queue

While delete queue not empty

‚Ä¶.Pull the next pointer from the delete queue as current record

‚Ä¶.If current record not marked

‚Ä¶‚Ä¶..Add all pointers to the delete queue

‚Ä¶‚Ä¶..Free all the storage fields

‚Ä¶‚Ä¶..Mark current record for deletion

Sweep the record heap freeing all marked records

Access to fields

The field access operator is . followed by the name of a field.

name\( = P@.name\)

Procedure Fields / methods

DEF RECobject

A%

B%

DEF PROCmethod1(a%,b%) // LOCAL vars and params must not have the same name as a record field!

A%=a%-b%

B%=a%+b%

ENDPROC

DEF FNfunc1‚Ä¶.

DEF PROCmethod2‚Ä¶‚Ä¶

ENDREC

Usage of procedure fields:

R@ = NEW RECobject // alternetive syntax choice for creating a new record, makes it explicit that record allocation is taking place.

R@.PROCmethod1(56,99)

q = R@.FNfunc1

Record Extension and overrides

DEF RECparent(args)

name$

DEF PROCmethod1:ENDPROC // an empty method, calling it does nothing, acts as a placeholder for later redefinition.

DEF PROCmethod2(blah%)

// Some code here

ENDPROC

DEF PROCmethod3(blah%)

// Some other code here

ENDPROC

DEF PROCmethod4:UNDEFINED:ENDPROC ‚Äî an undefined method placeholder, calling it throws an error, must redefine, like abstract in other languages.

ENDREC

DEF RECchild1(args) EXTEND RECparent(arg exprs) // allows inherited fields to be initialised/dimensioned

address$ // a new field

DEF PROCmethod1 // this overrides any method with the same name, implements something for method1.

// Do something

ENDPROC

// PROCmethod2 is not defined here, so the one from the parent is inherited.

DEF PROCmethod3(blah%) // overrides PROCmethod3

// Do this

PARENT.PROCmethod3(blah%+8) ‚Äî here we call PROCmethod3 from the parent.

// Do That

ENDPROC

DEF PROCmethod4 // this defines PROCmethod4 for the first time.

// Do something. Calling PARENT.method4 here throws an error (default halt program)

ENDPROC

ENDREC

PARENT

// passes control to an overridden method, that method may have been inherited through several levels of extension, it will activate the last matching definition.

THIS

// refers to the current object within a method, it is implied when accessing fields within methods.

TYPE$

// refers to the type of a record as a string e.g. ‚ÄúRECchild1‚Äù

TYPE

// refers to the type of the record internal representation, can be used for type tests

IF THIS.TYPE = RECchild1 THEN ‚Ä¶

TYPE and TYPE$ work on any pointer variable as well. to allow type comparisons (compare 2 pointers or pointer against TYPE value):

IF R@.TYPE = P@.TYPE // do they have the same dynamic type?

IF R@.TYPE <> RECsometype // R@ is NOT pointing to a RECsometype?

IF R@.TYPE > P@.TYPE // is R@ pointing to a supertype of P@?

IF R@.TYPE >= P@.TYPE // is R@ the same OR a supertype of P@?

IF R@.TYPE < RECparent // is R@ a subtype of RECparent?

IF R@.TYPE <= RECparent // is R@ the same as or a subtype of RECparent?

Calling an undefined method is a fatal error and will halt the program.

Fields are not redefined/overridden and must only be named once in an extension chain.

There is no multiple inheritance, interfaces, generics as these are complex and hard to do correctly.

Managing Namespace Pollution and example of ‚Äúclass‚Äù var/method

If a program has a large number of record types with lots of internal fields and methods that the user of the record does not need to touch the interface becomes a confusing mess.

Most OOP languages allow marking fields and methods as private/public, etc

I propose that for the BASIC extension above that all fields and methods are private by default and only visible inside the REC structure and by any child REC that extends from it.

To make things visible to the program at large, fields and methods are marked with an export mark ‚Äò<-‚Äô

DEF RECobject

<- A% // A% is visible to the whole program as MyPtr@.A%

B% // B% is only visible to methods inside RECobject fatal error to attempt access outside.

<- STATIC C% // this is global to all instances of RECobject

<- DEF PROCmethod1(a%,b%) // Can be called anywhere as MyPtr@.PROCmethod1(‚Ä¶)

A%=a%-b%

B%=a%+b%

ENDPROC

DEF FNfunc1 // Can be called inside PROCmethod1 or PROCmethod2 or FNfunc1 as THIS.FNfunc1(‚Ä¶) or PARENT.FNfunc1 (if inherited)

= C%

<- DEF PROCmethod2 // Can be called anywhere as MyPtr@.PROCmethod2(‚Ä¶)

A% = THIS.FNfunc1

ENDPROC

<- STATICDEF PROCdouble // affects all instances, can be called without any live instance

C% = C% * 2 // Can only manipulate STATIC fields and call STATIC methods/functions

ENDPROC

ENDREC

The exported API of this REC is:

DEF RECobject

<- A% // A% is visible to the whole program as MyPtr@.A%

<- STATIC C% // this is global to all instances of RECobject

<- DEF PROCmethod1(a%,b%) // Can be called anywhere as MyPtr@.PROCmethod1(‚Ä¶)

<- DEF PROCmethod2 // Can be called anywhere as MyPtr@.PROCmethod2(‚Ä¶)

<- STATICDEF PROCdouble // affects all instances, can be called without any live instance

ENDREC

Example usage outside the definition

RECobject.C% = 5 // set the class var C% to 5 for all RECobjects

R@ = NEW RECobject

R@.PROCmethod1(20,10)

PRINT R@.A% // prints 10

R@.PROCmethod2

PRINT R@.A% // prints 5

DEL R@ // delete the record

RECobject.PROCdouble // there are no live instances at this time

p@ = NEW RECobject

p@.PROCmethod1(100, 15)

PRINT p@.A% // prints 85

p@.PROCmethod2

PRINT p@.A% // prints 10, as C% was doubled by PROCdouble

DEL p@ // delete the record

Sorry about the terrible formatting, the forum editor wipes indentation.

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/2/topics/20102

Boot RISC OS Pi on Pi 4 from MSD

(date: 2025-11-02)

You could try reformatting the card, downloading the RISC OS Open Raspberry Pi card image ‚Äì it‚Äôs the first item here:

https://www.riscosopen.org/content/downloads/raspberry‚Ä¶

and imaging it to the reformatted card. You‚Äôll need a USB SD card reader but these are readily and cheaply obtainable. You‚Äôll also need disc-imaging software ‚Äì as it happens Raspberry Pi do a perfectly good one:

https://raspberrytips.com/raspberry-pi-imager-guide/

You can‚Äôt simply copy the diskimage to the card, the card must be imaged, hence the need for imager software (apologies if you already know all this, I can‚Äôt estimate your capability from the original post). Good luck, HTH.

Learning BASIC

(date: 2025-11-01)

Last year I spent many ‚Äòhappy‚Äô months writing these short guides. Having taught English abroad for 13 years I learned the hazards of ‚Äòteacher talk‚Äô and as you can see these volumes contain only code, with some image [usually of what the code produces on screen], but without the usual waffle most other programming books contain.

The title ‚ÄòThe Happy Hacker‚Äô was inspired by a song of the same name written by Chris Jeffers for the Alto computer over at Xerox PARC. [ https://soundcloud.com/audimprove/happy-hacker and https://vimeo.com/111334072].

Last week I reviewed all of the code and came up with one small improvement:

Rotate {Volume 1, page 12}

‚Ä¶

REPEAT

MOUSE x,y,button

‚Ä¶

ELSE

WAIT <‚Äî‚Äî‚Äî-add this to smooth rotation!

PROCplot_points

PROCrotate

PROCplot_points

ENDIF

UNTIL button <> 0

The original does NOT contain the ‚ÄòWAIT‚Äô command ‚Äì it still works but not smoothly.

I also made some additional content, not yet included in this Happy Hacker series, which I may include in ‚ÄòVolume 14‚Äô one day.

Thanks for that. It looks like we‚Äôre mostly aligned. Keeping the non-RISC OS 5 clearly marked in the wiki helps avoid any confusion for people (notably developers) who are downloading RISC OS 5 from elsewhere on our site, or looking at the sources in our repo.

I would say that you announcing things or presenting things is great, but it isn‚Äôt equivalent to contacting us directly or even posting in the Code Review forum to discuss anything that will consume shared identifiers or flags. ROLL unfortunately doesn‚Äôt have the people or the bandwidth to proactively track everything going on in all the RISC OS-community and adjacent projects. If we‚Äôve given mixed messages in the past, then I apologise for that.

That aside, it‚Äôs great to see people actively thinking about and working on paths that move RISC OS forward and out of the current 32-bit only shackles.

(date: 2025-10-29)

Wakefield RISC OS Computer Club

Meeting on Wednesday 5th November at 7.45pm

Martin Avison: Pluto

Martin will explain the background to Pluto, demonstrate a new install of Pluto and AntiSpam, send and receive some emails, and finally demonstrate a fully populated Pluto and some of its facilities.

This ‚Äòvirtual‚Äô meeting is open to all, and will take place using the Zoom conferencing service using our regular meeting credentials. Zoom invitations will be sent out ahead of the meeting, but only to those who email info2025@wrocc.org.uk to request one. If you would like to be part of the meeting (and don‚Äôt already have the link from a previous meeting or receive an invite in the next 24 hours as a member of WROCC), please RSVP ‚Äî at the latest by the end of Tuesday 4th November (GMT). We email the links out on the morning of the meeting.

If you haven‚Äôt used Zoom before, we suggest that before Wednesday you try to join the Zoom test meeting at https://zoom.us/test on the device that you intend to use, in order to check that your system works OK. You will not require a Zoom account to take part.

Past Meetings

Videos of previous meetings can be found in our links to past meetings at https://www.wrocc.org.uk/meetings

Club Membership

Annual membership of WROCC is available for those living near and far at 10.00ukp per year.

Members receive:

Creatng an ebook - 'part 2'

(date: 2025-10-26)

I‚Äôm now asking for info wrt a slightly different situation where I want to be able to make an ebook from a set of numbered jpeg files, one per page.

This is to generate ‚Äòde-oxidised‚Äô versions of PDFs of ancient pulp mags/paperbacks and render them in a far easier form to read.

I can export the jpegs OK. I can also write a Composcript to generate a new set of jpegs that have been ‚Äòde-browned‚Äô. But I then need to put those into a new PDF with one jpeg per page. The result then to be more easily read using the usual ebook reading progs on my natty tablet device. (I‚Äôll probably also greyscale the pages in most cases if they‚Äôre ‚Äòcolour‚Äô jpegs with black text on the brown of oxidised pulp paper.

I don‚Äôt mind if the process has to take some time to chug though hundreds of jpegs, I can get a cup of single-estate tea and a biscuit as my RO box does the job. Problem at present is that some anient pulp mags/books are almost unreadable due to becoming oxidised and the the PDF /ebook maker didn‚Äôt bother to deal with that. But I suspect a tool like this would be very handy for anyone who wants to read material that exhibits this problem.

And I suspect that for me this RO approach will be easier than trying to work out how to automate the process on Linux as I already know how to use !Compo, etc, for the actual processing. Just not the bit where the resulting bitmaps need to be packed into a PDF (‚Ä¶or other ebook format? Is there one that just ‚Äòzips‚Äô the pages with some meta-info to guide ebook rendering? That might be handy!)

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/11/topics/20077

!Chess 1.30 released

(date: 2025-10-26)

The archive has lost the filetypes: they‚Äôre added as an extension to the filenames. But it‚Äôs easy to change that, though. Thank you for the update.

The archive on the release page is a risc os zip file, if unzipped inside risc os using sparkplug/infozip/sparkfs etc, the filetypes are present. Do not unzip this archive using linux/mac/windows zip software, as the filetype information will be lost.

https://www.riscosopen.org/forum/forums/1/topics/19904

(date: 2025-10-24)

In last minute stop-press news, RISCOSbits are pleased to announce a few additions to the London Show stand.

For those of you who are in the market for a RISC OS laptop, RISCOSbits may have exactly what you are looking for at the London show! We will have VERYLIMITED stock of Linux enabled, but RISC OS capable Pinebook Pros available for sale at the London show. Whilst these laptops are not fitted with RISC OS for licencing reasons, we can demonstrate them running RISC OS to show you that it is possible and easy to do. All you will need to do is pop along to another stand at the show and purchase access to the ROM.

As people may be aware, there are two variants of Pinebook Pro ‚Äì one with a UK layout keyboard, and one with a more generic (US) layout. We will have the latter available.

The Pinebook Pro comes equipped with 64GB of eMMC storage preinstalled and pre-formatted for RISC OS use. The laptops (running Linux) will be available on a ‚Äúfirst come, first served‚Äù basis for only ¬£150 ‚Äì remember, stocks are very limited. We also have a super bargain special offer on one with a slight donk on the top rim of the shell. Doesn‚Äôt affect the functionality, but we‚Äôll knock a further ¬£25 off!

Our next bit of exclusive news is we‚Äôll be selling external antennas for Compute Module 4 systems, especially those in metal cases. Many of you will be aware that the Linux method of enabling this using dtparams doesn‚Äôt work on RISC OS, but by partnering with Stader Software, we are able to offer exclusive free access to antenna control software for RISC OS to enable the external antenna.

As an added bonus, if you buy a system with a WiFi- enabled Compute Module 4 from our FreeNVMe or FAST range and you ask for an antenna, we‚Äôll give it you for free, including exclusive access to the control software for RISC OS. Combine this with our ‚ÄòGet In Free*‚Äô offer and you‚Äôre making incredible savings! It‚Äôs also worth remembering we publish the prices and specifications of our systems on our website so you can calculate the bang per buck you get with RISCOSbits!

We‚Äôll also have a few gold and black case badges to tell the world what‚Äôs running inside your otherwise anonymous case! And at a pocket money price of only ¬£2.50!

And the final teaser is we‚Äôll be bringing along some delightful Welsh slate drinks mats, engraved with your favourite OS logo. Available for just ¬£5 each, they‚Äôre sure to make your desk look oh so pretty and er, ringless. You could even buy a set of four for ¬£18 for your coffee table or home cocktail bar!

RCI Hardware at London Show - 20ukp off too

(date: 2025-10-24)

  • We‚Äôll be knocking 20ukp off all hardware items (over 50ukp) at the show.

    You don‚Äôt need to quote any adverts or phrases or claim anything special.

    Just money off for everyone :) **

At the recent Show Preview user group meeting, Andrew Rawnsley of RCI

demonstrated some new hardware items that had been proving popular this

summer, and will be available at the London Show this weekend.

18 inches of RISCBook

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=

First up was a new 18" RISCBook laptop. For those unfamiliar, the

RISCBook range of laptops run RISC OS and Windows together, providing the

best of both RISC OS and Windows software, with links between the two OSs

to allow them to share resources such as files, printers, clipboard, and

networking.

The pressing onset of Windows 11 has prompted a number of users to upgrade

this Autumn, and the 18" laptop has proven popular. Although 18" may

sound huge for a laptop, screen shapes have become more flexible in recent

times, and the 18" uses a 16:10 ratio with more vertical space for

documents. This means it is roughly the same size/weight as a 17" laptop,

whilst offering more screen space (1920√ó1200). Very practical for working

on documents, and the high refresh rate (144 Hz) IPS panel looks lovely.

We‚Äôve found that as people age, they appreciate the larger screens and

full size backlit keyboards (with number pads), whilst finding the

convenience of a laptop is easier to fit in various rooms. For example,

RCI‚Äôs Allan (Andrew‚Äôs father) now uses his laptop downstairs to save

having to trek up to the more traditional machines in his office upstairs.

Whilst the laptops aren‚Äôt RISC OS friendly when they arrive, RCI is able

to adapt them to run RISC OS beautifully, with smooth performance and

flexible software compatibility (run both 26bit and 32bit applications).

Touchpad mouse gestures (eg. 3 finger tap) mean that replication of the

three button mouse is great too. Of course, you can plug in a mouse (or

use a wireless one) too.

These laptops are no slouches ‚Äì 8-core, 16 thread AMD chips amply

demonstrate why AMD have become so dominant again recently ‚Äì they can

motor through anything from web browsing to video editing. Whilst the

graphics are on-chip, they‚Äôre top tier for what they are, making games

possible too. With 16GB RAM and 1TB of storage packed into a slim and

low-weight chassis, there‚Äôs a lot of ‚Äúoomph‚Äù inside.

Of course, RCI offers a range of other RISCBooks too, from 13" upwards

with a variety of screens including OLED. However, these 18" units have

proven quite popular, and so we‚Äôre singling them out to RISC OS users.

The laptops should be on display in London. Expect to see RCI‚Äôs MiniPC

range too.

Pinebook Pros

=-=-=-=-=-=-=

Speaking of Laptops, RCI still have one or two Pinebook Pros ‚Äì they grab

stock from around the world when they appear online. Pinebook Pros offer

a fantastic native-RISC OS experience with class leading performance,

working wifi, and even optional NVMe sockets for high speed storage.

Prices fluctuate as limited availability often results in price spikes,

but RCI is trying to keep prices in the same ballpark as before.

N.Ex.T, Hydra and NVMe

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RCI will also be showing N.Ex.T and Hydra systems as usual ‚Äì expect to see

large NVMe drives and some exciting new features. See the latest v9 (and

the forthcoming v10) NVMe drivers with SMART disc health features and

drive health checks. See native RISC OS disc partitions, 4K sectors, our

NVMe toolkit and more.

Hydra shows how Pi4 and Pi5 tech can be used side-by-side, and you‚Äôll be

able to see ROD‚Äôs new RISC OS Direct for Pi5 running on a Hydra Head.

Check out the tiny mini.pi N.Ex.T computer which packs almost every

feature into the tiniest box, at a cracking price.

There will also be some rather different devices shown with up to 8 NVMe

slots! Aimed at file sharing and home NAS appliances, these small silent

boxes provide exceptional capabilities at surprisingly affordable prices,

whilst opening up a range of options for RISC OS and allowing room to

expand and grow. Come and find out more at the show.

RISCube Minis

=-=-=-=-=-=-=

We‚Äôve talked about RISCBooks, but 2025 has also bee the year of MiniPCs

with our range of RISCube Minis offering state of the art features and

stunning performance at lower-than-ever prices. See features like the

latest USB4, multiple 4K+ displays, Wifi 6E and 7, 2.5 Gbit ethernet and

more ‚Äì all useable from RISC OS!

Monitors

=-=-=-=-

We‚Äôll have a selection of IPS and OLED displays available on the stand for

you to check out and plan the best way to make your day-to-day computing

more pleasurable. Remember your screen determines everything you see and

do on the computer, so if you‚Äôre an enthusiast (and coming to a computer

show counts as an enthusiast!) then you deserve the best you can.

Monitor prices have come down a bit recently, so why not take advantage of

that to treat yourself?

Whatever takes your fancy, come and check out our range at the RCI stand

at the show and say hello!

Show Offer

(date: 2025-10-24)

The 368 page Impression User Manual (in the form of a PDF file) was originally provided free to purchasers of Impression X. This User Manual is now available in electronic form free to all users of Impression Style (which is free to download from !Store), Publisher and Publisher Plus from !Store.

A printed version of the manual is still available, normal price ¬£25, which includes a personal download link for Impression Publisher Plus version 5.13, courtesy of RISC OS Developments. I shall be discounting the few remaining copies of this manual at the show.

Although the User Manual was created in Impression, with contents and index created automatically, the PDF that was produced was designed to produce a printed manual. It therefore has no internal links. The RingBind version of the User Manual does have page to page links from the Contents pages, section to section and all 12 pages of the Index.

I shall be handing out USB sticks at the show free of charge with the latest version of !FamTree, version 1.58 (May 2024) [which will be made free to download from !Store after the show]. The USB sticks are only 32Mbytes so you can have as much of the other software listed below as will fit ‚Äì for example a RingBind version of the RISC OS 5.30 User Manual (with over 3000 internal links) or both RingBind and PDF versions of the Impression User Manual. If you want more then I‚Äôll put it on your own USB stick or another 32MB stick. No individual zip file is larger than 14Mbytes. At least until stocks run out‚Ä¶

This amounts to over 242M bytes of data all on a 128Mbyte USB stick.

London is closer than you think

(date: 2025-10-23)

This year‚Äôs London show organised by ROUGOL is this Saturday the 25th October from 11am. Shows are the perfect opportunity to meet and talk to fellow RISC OS users and developers about what they‚Äôre doing with our favourite operating system.

Venue details

A short distance by public transport, around ten miles from Heathrow airport, less than four miles from the M1 motorway, the Harrow District Masonic Centre is closer than you think; see this Google map for directions.

Please note: engineering work means the Bakerloo tube line is closed this weekend.

See BASIC in action

See the alpha version of BBCBASIC rewritten in C, running natively on both RISC OS 5 and Windows x64, and find out what‚Äôs required to get it all finished. It‚Äôs a considerable technical effort, and will pave the way for all kinds of language extensions in future.

Want to know why nightly builds of BASIC gained a new SYS-as-a-function keyword recently? It‚Äôs all part of the mission to the moon.

https://www.riscosopen.org/news/articles/2025/10/23/london-is-closer-than-you-think

NetFetch 6 new available

(date: 2025-10-23)

R-Comp are launching version 6 of NetFetch at the London show, over six years since v5.5 launched at Wakefield 2019.

(Spoiler ‚Äì it‚Äôs live now on !Store)

NetFetch provides flexible mail and news fetching for RISC OS, including anti spam and other filtering capabilities, as well as a friendly front end to RISC OS internet-related software. A version of Messenger Pro is included to provide users with a ‚Äúready to use‚Äù kit.

Since the release of v5.5, email provision has changed quite substantially. Many more ISPs require enhanced security in a variety of forms ‚Äì more passwords and logins, more SSL/TLS encryption, greater identity checks and so on. NetFetch 6 recognises this and has revamped its configuration to emphasise the features that modern people require. New and returning users will find that setting up NetFetch 6 is considerably improved, especially with modern ISPs.

These improvements have been brought about because internet providers such as Orpheus and Plusnet have both undergone changes recently, and whilst helping user sort out their problems, we discovered various areas that

needed to be improved or made clearer. Version six reflects these, modernising and improving the experience.

News handling has also seen a revamp, as many ISPs no longer offer newsgroup facilities. Those that do often require username/password login, so the old setup routines no longer made sense. We have now taken news out of the initial setup to streamline things, and instead introduced a new Assistant to guide people through setting up free newsgroup access regardless of ISP. By following the built-in assistant, and filling out two boxes, you‚Äôll be able to get newsgroup access set up whenever you‚Äôre ready. Meanwhile, existing users will appreciate clearer settings, and easy support for both server login and SSL/TLS.

Speaking of encryption, v6 sees support added for the latest TLS 1.3 standard including handshake-level identity checks. These are conducted as part of the TLS connection to prove you are who you say you are ‚Äì something that we have seen mandated on real-world ‚Äúbig company‚Äù TLS 1.3 servers.

NetFetch 6 will be available as a paid-for upgrade to existing customers, launching at the London show, but anyone who has purchased v5.5 this year (2025) can claim a free upgrade by specifying their purchase date when

ordering. Version 6 will be available in person at the show and via !Store download.

NetFetch 6 costs 35ukp new, with upgrades costing 20ukp either in person or via !Store. The new version is live now on !Store and as with its predecessor, includes free updates for the foreseeable future (6 years again? Can‚Äôt promise, but who knows!).

Best wishes,

Andrew

Free entry at the London Show 2025 with RISCOSbits*

(date: 2025-10-23)

*it‚Äôs okay, ROUGOL, we‚Äôre not sneaking people in through a side entrance!

To celebrate the first show outing of our updated and very latest release of FreeNVMe genuinely open source drivers, RISCOSbits are offering to refund people‚Äôs entrance fee, by way of an extra discount on all purchases of NVMe-enabled pre-built systems at our stand.

Terms and conditions obviously apply (we‚Äôll only offer one refund per customer) but we‚Äôre happy if you get together with a RISC OS friend and send your mate up to buy another NVMe system on your behalf to get a second discount!

Simply quote ‚ÄòOi! Gimme my door money back‚Äô when making your purchase and we‚Äôll knock it off the price!

About FreeNVMe

FreeNVMe is the next generation of fully Open Source RISC OS storage technology and it‚Äôs completely free!

As the result of partnering with Stader Softwareentwicklung and RISC OS Open, RISCOSbits have been instrumental in developing, and further updating, the free and fully Open Source NVMe driver and filing system, that we first demonstrated way back in December 2023. And it has been in reliable use on RISCOSbits‚Äô Compute Module 4 systems ever since.

Designed from the ground up to fit perfectly with existing RISC OS filesystems, FreeNVMe follows all the usual filecore conventions so that all existing tools, such as DiscKnight, work straight out of the box ‚Äì no custom tools are required.

A conscious decision was made to adopt the existing standards for filing systems, so that any developments to the core of RISC OS would automatically integrate with FreeNVMe.

There‚Äôs no tie-in to a paid-for support scheme ‚Äì our driver is designed to work with the nightly builds from RISC OS Open. And it‚Äôs completely free. You can download it now, without having to buy a system, an NVMe drive or anything else:

www.riscosbits.co.uk/nvme/

https://www.riscosopen.org/content/downloads/raspberry‚Ä¶

And FreeNVMe is genuinely open source. You can look at, and download, the source code directly from the RISC OS Open repository NOW. You have the opportunity to contribute to the code to improve FreeNVMe and make it into the real community-led filing system it was intended to be.

FreeNVMe is designed to offer the following features as standard:

  • Works on Raspberry Pi Compute Module 4 systems
  • 4Kn sectors to allow for drives up to 2TB
  • Partitioning via freely available software
  • DiscKnight compatibility
  • Standard file system icon (no separate app needed)
  • Dual format drives with separate icons for each format.

And FreeNVMe is FAST! So fast that we felt comfortable incorporating it into our premium range of computers without any hidden charges.

What‚Äôs New

In our latest developments, rather than chasing irrelevant numbers, we‚Äôve been focusing on real-world usability and integration ‚Äì from more reliable file handling and faster boot times to improved support for large storage volumes and smoother performance under pressure. At the show, you‚Äôll be able to see how NVMe, when properly harnessed, makes RISC OS feel more modern, stable, and capable than ever before. We‚Äôve also improved drive compatibility to near 100% ‚Äì there‚Äôll always be rogue drives, but we‚Äôve even built in a system to manage them.

We don‚Äôt need to make strangely calculated claims about how it compares to other products ‚Äì we just give it to you for nothing so you can make your own mind up!

PhotoDesk 3.25 released

(date: 2025-10-23)

We are pleased to announce that version 3.25 of PhotoDesk is now available to download for existing users via !Store.

Following on from 3.24‚Äôs colossal number of changes, 3.25 is a much smaller affair, correcting a few things that slipped through and have been reported since:

  • ‚Äúclick_in_rotate‚Äù routine called ‚Äúclick_in_draw‚Äù with the incorrect number of paramters. Now fixed.

  • Resize and Rotate functions had Bi-cubic and Bi-linear modes swapped. Expected operation has been restored.

  • PNG files were being saved without compression, leading to very large files. Since PNG compression is lossless, this was not sensible, so PNGs are now compressed as you‚Äôd expect.

The update is available as a free download for anyone who purchased the XAT edition (3.18+) of PhotoDesk some years ago.

We will have a number of fresh CDs with 3.25 on at the London Show this weekend. We offer them as very low cost ‚Äústocking stuffers‚Äù for existing users. The CDs contain extra software (3.25 adds Chris Terran‚Äôs GradGrind palette editor designed for use with PhotoDesk) that wouldn‚Äôt fit in the regular download, plus extras like full sets of example images and documentation etc.

If you don‚Äôt have a CD drive, bring a USB stick (we do sell them, but they tend to be larger ones) and we‚Äôll copy the CD contents onto the stick for you.

Best wishes,

Andrew
